# 296\n
{Edinburgh, Royal College of Physicians, MS of Cursor Mundi, hand C, fols. 37r-50v}\n
C14a\n
460 452 N\n
{=York=}\n
{=Sample represents all the English in this hand. The extracts from\n
Cursor Mundi in this MS are imperfect and wrongly ordered. Hand C\n
provides the earlier portions, Cursor Mundi lines 18989-22417 (with\n
gaps). Hand A provides some later portions while between the two\n
contributions Hand B provides some of the Northern Homily Collection.\n
This hand\'s contribution begins in Morris\'s edition vol. 5 (1878), Appendix\n
1, p. 1587=}\n
{=Script - a small neat Textura=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=Thorn is thorn-shaped not <y>-shaped. The scribe only seems to\n
use the littera \'y\' in names eg YSAAC, but it is clear from this\n
that he does distinguish their shapes. Otherwise, the avoidance\n
of \'y\' is very deliberate, for vocalic [i] he always uses <i> and\n
for [j] he uses <g>. Punctuation is virtually absent except on fol.\n
38r where the scribe has a punctus at every line end. He does not\n
however keep this up beyond the recto of the folio. On this folio also\n
he ornaments the ascenders of the letters on the top line and the\n
descenders of the letters on the bottom line. Again this seems to be a\n
temporary flight of fancy. Occasionally, if the last word of a line\n
will not fit the column width and has to be taken to the end of the\n
line below or above, a punctus is used to divide it from the text\n
belonging to the other line. Where this happens the punctus is\n
included and its use explained. Punctus on either side of capital <I>\n
are taken to be part of the figura and are ignored. In his edition\n
Morris expands the usual abbreviation for <er> either as <ir> or <er>\n
according to the word. Here I always expand, as with our normal\n
practice, as <er>. The same abbreviation (a hook above the preceding\n
letter) is used after A as an abbreviation for "and". Here I follow\n
what I did in language 2 of the Cotton Owl and the Nightingale and\n
transcribe A~. A similar hook is sometimes used stem finally, and is\n
realised in the same way, e.g. ELL~ rather than ELLes or ELLis. The\n
scribe usually has the same yogh-shaped symbol for yogh and <z> which\n
I realise always as yogh i.e. lower case <z>. Where it is <z>-shaped\n
it is realised as Z=}\n

{=Here for the next 246 lines, the Edinburgh text is used by Morris to\n
fill a gap in his edition of the Trinity version running parallel to\n
Cotton, Fairfax and Gottingen. See vol iv (EETS OS 66 (1877) pp. 1237-51).\n
Morris\'s editorial procedures are therefore different for this stretch,\n
the abbrevations usually being expanded silently. I continue to notice\n
substantive errors or misprints in Morris\'s text but I do not note\n
in this 246-line stretch those occasions where he fails to italicise\n
abbrevations=}\n

!_BA~\n
{=Morris (1878) transcribes this BAer. But given that the abbreviation is the\n
same one used in different contexts for <er>, <nd> (in "and"), <is> or\n
<es> in verbal endings etc. It is not certain what it represents here.\n
The word is not present in the other versions and if if is read BAer it\n
could conceivably be for the adjective "bare" or the noun "boar". But\n
arguably it could indicate BArn. I have not attempted to tag the word\n
unless and until a similar use of the abbreviation in another context\n
may give a clue. The word in in any case metrically redundant and is not\n
needed by the sense=}\n

$stecan{*}/vi{rh}_STECK+E $/vi{rh}_+E\n
{"decide?"}\n
{=The meaning of this passage is unclear to me though the general gist\n
is obvious. A literal translation is "to be found so shall he stick"\n
which does not seem to make much sense given the next clause. Gottingen\n
has the same wording. Fairfax and Trinity paraphrase to make sense but\n
each choose a different way out, suggesting scribal editing. Cotton has\n
STERCK perhaps written for STRECK "move quickly" which fits better with\n
jumping over hills. See Morris (1892) vol VI, notes who thinks "streak"\n
is probably the correct reading and who provides a very loose paraphrase\n
for this passage=}\n
